<p>The world's top selling highway-capable electric car ever is the <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a>, released in December 2010, with global sales of 49,117 units through December 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Sales2Yrs_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sales2Yrs-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TopSellingEver_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopSellingEver-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by the <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_family" title="Mitsubishi i-MiEV family" class="mw-redirect">Mitsubishi i-MiEV family</a>, with global sales of about 24,000 cars sold or exported since 2009 through December 2012, which includes 5,017 Peugeot iOns and 4,977 Citroën C-Zeros rebadged and sold in the European market.<sup id="cite_ref-iMiEVGlobal_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iMiEVGlobal-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JapMiEV09_12_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapMiEV09_12-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EUsales2011_12_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUsales2011_12-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> The third best selling highway-capable all-electric vehicle is the Renault Kangoo Z.E. utility van, with global sales of 6.665 units since October 2011 through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesRnlt2011_12_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesRnlt2011_12-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There are also several pre-production models and plug-in conversions of existing <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> models undergoing field trials or are part of demonstration programs, such as the <a href="/wiki/Audi_A1_e-tron" title="Audi A1 e-tron" class="mw-redirect">Audi A1 e-tron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_BlueOn" title="Hyundai BlueOn">Hyundai BlueOn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_A-Class_E-Cell" title="Mercedes A-Class E-Cell" class="mw-redirect">Mercedes A-Class E-Cell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scion_iQ_EV" title="Scion iQ EV" class="mw-redirect">Scion iQ EV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tata_Indica_Vista_EV" title="Tata Indica Vista EV" class="mw-redirect">Tata Indica Vista EV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf_blue-e-motion" title="Volkswagen Golf blue-e-motion" class="mw-redirect">Volkswagen Golf blue-e-motion</a>. Models scheduled for market launch in 2013 and 2014 include the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_e-Up!" title="Volkswagen e-Up!" class="mw-redirect">Volkswagen e-Up!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Electric_SP.01" title="Detroit Electric SP.01" class="mw-redirect">Detroit Electric SP.01</a>, <a href="/wiki/BMW_i3" title="BMW i3">BMW i3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_B-Class_Electric_Drive" title="Mercedes-Benz B-Class Electric Drive" class="mw-redirect">Mercedes-Benz B-Class Electric Drive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_X" title="Tesla Model X">Tesla Model X</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Infiniti_LE" title="Infiniti LE">Infiniti LE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVTracker_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVTracker-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_cars_by_country">Electric cars by country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Electric cars by country">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Electric cars by country" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_car_use_by_country" title="Electric car use by country">Electric car use by country</a></div>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Plug-in electric vehicles in the United Kingdom">Plug-in electric vehicles in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>As of December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Japan and the United States are the largest highway-capable electric car country markets in the world, followed by several <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western European</a> countries and China. Pure electric car sales in 2012 were led by Japan with a 28% <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of global sales, followed by the United States with a 26% share, China with 16%, France with 11%, and Norway with 7%.<sup id="cite_ref-Outlook2013_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Outlook2013-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In Japan, more than 28,000 all-electric cars electric cars have been sold through December 2012, with sales led by the Nissan Leaf with about 21,000 units sold since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-LeafSalesJAP_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeafSalesJAP-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> Around 27,000 all-electric cars have been sold in the U.S. since 2008, and sales are led by the Nissan Leaf, with 19,512 units sold through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVUSales2012_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVUSales2012-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PEVsalesUS0712_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVsalesUS0712-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG/220px-Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG/330px-Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG/440px-Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bilbao_05_2012_Opel_Ampera_2472.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The Opel Ampera is the top selling plug-in electric car in Europe for 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TopEUAmpera_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopEUAmpera-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 2010, a total of 37,380 electric-drive passenger cars have been sold in Western European countries through December 2012, with yearly sales climbing from 1,614 all-electric cars in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-EUsales10_12_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUsales10_12-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> to 11,563 electric cars during 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-SalesEurope2011_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesEurope2011-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> to reach 24,203 plug-in electric cars in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesEurope2012_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesEurope2012-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of plug-in electric cars rose from 0.09% of all new car sales in the region in 2011 to 0.2% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesEurope2011_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesEurope2011-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesEurope2012_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesEurope2012-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sales during these two years were led by the Nissan Leaf with 6,938 units, followed by the Peugeot iOn with 5,017 units, and the Citroën C-Zero with 4,977 cars sold. When electric vehicles with range extender plug-in hybrids are considered, the Opel/Vauxhall Ampera ranks second after the Leaf with 5,572 units delivered in Europe since late 2011 through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-EUsales2011_12_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUsales2011_12-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> The top selling models in the region in 2011 were the Mitsubishi i-MiEV (2,608) followed by its rebadged versions the Peugeot iOn (1,926) and the Citroën C-Zero (1,830).<sup id="cite_ref-EUsales2011_12_253-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUsales2011_12-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesEurope2011_262-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesEurope2011-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> The Opel/Vauxhall Ampera was Europe's top selling electric-drive car in 2012 with 5,210 units representing a market share of 21.5% of the region's electric passenger car segment.<sup id="cite_ref-EUsales2011_12_253-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUsales2011_12-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TopEUAmpera_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TopEUAmpera-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> The Nissan Leaf ranked second with 5,029 electric cars sold for a market share of 20.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-EUsales2011_12_253-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUsales2011_12-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> The top selling country markets in 2011 were France (2,630), Norway (2,240), Germany (2,154), and the United Kingdom (1,082).<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2011_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2011-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UKsales2011_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKsales2011-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, the leading countries were France (5,663),<sup id="cite_ref-SalesFR2010_13_238-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesFR2010_13-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> the Netherlands (5,093),<sup id="cite_ref-NetherPEV2012_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NetherPEV2012-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NetherSales2011_12_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NetherSales2011_12-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup> Norway (4,679),<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2012_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2012-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup> and Germany (2,956).<sup id="cite_ref-GerSales2012full_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GerSales2012full-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales in Germany, the Netherlands and Norway include plug-in hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-NetherPEV2012_246-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NetherPEV2012-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2012_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2012-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GerSales2012full_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GerSales2012full-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EU102012_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU102012-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> As of December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the leading countries in terms of EV penetration of the total auto fleet are Norway with 4 electric car per 1,000 automobiles registered in the country, Estonia with 1 electric car for every 1,000 cars, and the Netherlands with a penetration of 0.6 electric cars per 1,000 registered cars.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Japan</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:-Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/-Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG/220px--Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/-Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG/330px--Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/-Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG/440px--Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:-Nissan_Leaf_hino_koutsu.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Nissan Leaf operating as a taxi in Japan</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicles_in_Japan" title="Plug-in electric vehicles in Japan">Plug-in electric vehicles in Japan</a></div>
<p>Since July 2009, more than 28,000 all-electric cars have been sold in Japan through December 2012, representing a market share of 0.16% of total new car sales in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-JapMiEV09_12_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapMiEV09_12-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LeafSalesJAP_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeafSalesJAP-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Share2012_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Share2012-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> The Nissan Leaf is the market leader with about 21,000 units sold since December 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-LeafSalesJAP_257-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeafSalesJAP-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by the Mitsubishi i MiEV, launched for fleet customers in Japan in late July 2009, with cumulative sales of 7,233 i-MiEVs through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-JapMiEV09_12_252-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapMiEV09_12-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> Considering plug-in hybrids and electric utility vans, there were more than 41,000 <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicles</a> sold in the country through December 2012. This figure includes 3,234 <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Minicab_MiEV" title="Mitsubishi Minicab MiEV" class="mw-redirect">Minicab MiEV</a> electric utility vehicles sold since December 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-JapMiEV09_12_252-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapMiEV09_12-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> and 9,500 <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_PHV" title="Toyota Prius PHV" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Prius PHVs</a> sold between January and October 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-PiPSales1012_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PiPSales1012-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>United States</dt>
</dl>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicles_in_the_United_States" title="Plug-in electric vehicles in the United States">Plug-in electric vehicles in the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Model_S.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Model_S.jpg/220px-Model_S.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Model_S.jpg/330px-Model_S.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Model_S.jpg/440px-Model_S.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Model_S.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S</a> in the second best selling all-electric car in the U.S.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, around 27,000 all-electric cars have been sold in the U.S. since 2008, led by the Nissan Leaf, with 19,512 units sold through December 2012, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S</a> with 2,650 units sold through December 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Roadster" title="Tesla Roadster">Tesla Roadster</a>, which sold around 1,800 units until sales ended in the country in December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVUSales2012_241-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVUSales2012-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PEVsalesUS0712_258-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVsalesUS0712-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> As of August 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 32% of total electric car sales in the country took place in California,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> California leadership arises from being the most populous state and also the largest U.S car market with about 10% of all new car sales.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AEV_PHEV_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AEV_PHEV-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> Furthermore, the state provides the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Vehicle_Rebate_Project" title="Clean Vehicle Rebate Project" class="mw-redirect">Clean Vehicle Rebate</a> in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles#Federal_Government" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">federal tax credit</a>, and also has an air quality mandate that requires automakers to sell a combined 7,500 <a href="/wiki/Zero-emission_vehicle" title="Zero-emission vehicle" class="mw-redirect">zero-emission vehicles</a> (ZEVs) between 2012 and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Accounting for plug-in hybrid electric cars, the United States, as of December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, has the largest fleet of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicles</a> (PEVs) in the world, with more than 70,000 highway-capable plug-in electric cars sold since 2010, of which, 17,800 units were delivered during 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> and more than 53,000 during 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">Chevrolet Volt</a> plug-in hybrid is the top selling electric-drive car, with 31,458 units sold through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVUSales2012_241-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVUSales2012-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PEVsalesUS0712_258-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVsalesUS0712-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> During 2011, all-electric cars (10,064 sold) oversold plug-in hybrids (7,671 sold), but increased Volt sales, together with the introduction of the Prius PHV and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max" title="Ford C-Max">Ford C-Max</a>, allowed plug-in hybrids to take the lead over pure electric cars during 2012, with 38,584 PHEVs sold versus 14,251 BEVs.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> During the first quarter of 2013 a total of 17,813 PEVs were sold in the U.S., representing 0.53% share of total new car sales in the quarter. Sales were led by the Tesla Model S more than 4,750 units, followed by the Chevrolet Volt with 4,244 units, and the Nissan Leaf with 3,539 cars.<sup id="cite_ref-PEVSales2013US_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PEVSales2013US-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The U.S. government has pledged <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2.4 billion</span> in federal grants for electric cars and batteries.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>China</dt>
</dl>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electric_car_use_by_country#China" title="Electric car use by country">Electric cars in China</a></div>
<p>As of June 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 39,800 electric vehicles in <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">China</a>, up from 27,800 registered through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaEVs062013_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaEVs062013-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup> A total of 5,579 electric vehicles were sold in China during 2011, including passenger and commercial vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales in 2012 reached 12,791 units, which includes 11,375 all-electric vehicles and 1,416 plug-in hybrids, representing 0.07% of the country's total new car sales.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> The top-selling pure electric car in China for 2012 was the <a href="/wiki/Chery_QQ3_EV" title="Chery QQ3 EV" class="mw-redirect">Chery QQ3 EV</a> <a href="/wiki/City_car" title="City car">city car</a>, with 5,305 units sold, followed by the <a href="/wiki/JAC_J3_EV" title="JAC J3 EV" class="mw-redirect">JAC J3 EV</a> with 2,485 units, and the <a href="/wiki/BYD_e6" title="BYD e6">BYD e6</a> with 2,091 cars.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales during the first six months of 2013 totaled 5,889 units, including 5,114 pure electric vehicles and 775 plug-in hybrids, representing 0.05% of new car sales in the country during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-ChinaEVs062013_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChinaEVs062013-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>France</dt>
</dl>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electric_cars_in_France" title="Electric cars in France" class="mw-redirect">Electric cars in France</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG/220px-Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG/330px-Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG/440px-Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Renault_Zoe_on_MIAS_2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Renault_Zoe" title="Renault Zoe">Renault Zoe</a> was the top selling electric car in France during the first five months of 2013, and became best selling electric car since 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since January 2010, more than 14,600 highway-capable all-electric vehicles have been registered in France through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-FR1112_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FR1112-289"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_01_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_01-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> Of these, 8,477 are electric cars and 6,129 are electric utility vans.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesFR2010_13_238-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesFR2010_13-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_01_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_01-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> Electric car sales increased from 184 cars in 2010, through 2,630 units 2011, to 5,663 units in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesFR2010_13_238-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesFR2010_13-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesFr2011_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesFr2011-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> Sales of all-electric cars in 2012 increased 115% from 2011, and captured a market share of 0.3% of new car sales in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, 3,651 electric utility vans were registered in 2012, up from 1,683 in 2011, and 980 in 2010; increasing the total of highway-capable electric vehicles registered during 2012 to 9,314 units, and making France the leading European EV market in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_01_290-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_01-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_02_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_02-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, a total of 666 plug-in hybrids were registered during 2012, with sales led by the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius_PHV" title="Toyota Prius PHV" class="mw-redirect">Toyota Prius PHV</a> with 413 registrations and the Opel Ampera with 190.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG/220px-Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG/330px-Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG/440px-Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Autolib_06_2012_Bluecar_2905.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bollor%C3%A9_Bluecar" title="Bolloré Bluecar">Bolloré Bluecar</a>, deployed for the Parisian <a href="/wiki/Autolib%27" title="Autolib'">Autolib'</a><a href="/wiki/Carsharing" title="Carsharing">carsharing</a> program, led highway-capable electric car registrations in France in 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Electric car sales in the French market for 2011 were led by the Citroën C-Zero with 645 units followed by the Peugeot iOns with 639 vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesFr2011_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesFr2011-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> During 2012, all-electric car registrations in France were led by the <a href="/wiki/Bollor%C3%A9_Bluecar" title="Bolloré Bluecar">Bolloré Bluecar</a> with 1,543 units, the C-Zero with 1,409, and the iOn with 1,335, together representing 76% of all electric car sales that year.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Renault_Kangoo_Z.E." title="Renault Kangoo Z.E." class="mw-redirect">Renault Kangoo Z.E.</a> was the top selling utility electric vehicle with 2,869 units registered in 2012, representing a market share of 82% of the segment.<sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_01_290-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_01-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_02_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_02-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> A total of 3,652 Kangoo ZEs have been registered in France through December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-FRSales2012_01_290-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRSales2012_01-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Renault_Twizy" title="Renault Twizy">Renault Twizy</a> electric quadricycle, launched in March 2012, sold 2,232 units during 2012, surpassing the Bolloré Bluecar, the top selling highway-capable electric car, and ranking as the second best selling <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicle</a> after the Kangoo Z.E.<sup id="cite_ref-TwizySales_222-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TwizySales-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the first quarter of 2013, registrations of pure electric cars reached 2,248 units, led by the <a href="/wiki/Renault_Zoe" title="Renault Zoe">Renault Zoe</a> with 1,599 units representing 71% of total EV sales. Registrations of all-electric utility vans reached 1,275 units, led by the Renault Kangoo Z.E. with 1,051 units.<sup id="cite_ref-FR2011_13_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FR2011_13-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SalesQ12013_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesQ12013-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FR032013_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FR032013-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> Total registrations of all-electric cars since January 2010 through May 2013 are led by the Renault Zoe, with 2,878 units, followed by the Bolloré Bluecar, with 2,200 units, and the Peugeot iOn, with 2,139 units.<sup id="cite_ref-SalesFR2010_13_238-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SalesFR2010_13-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup><br style="clear:both;" /></p>
<dl>
<dt>Norway</dt>
</dl>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicles_in_Norway" title="Plug-in electric vehicles in Norway">Plug-in electric vehicles in Norway</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla.jpg/220px-Tesla.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla.jpg/330px-Tesla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tesla.jpg/440px-Tesla.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
Norway has the largest electric car ownership per capita in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwayLargest_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayLargest-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> Shown a <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Roadster" title="Tesla Roadster">Tesla Roadster</a>, a <a href="/wiki/REVAi" title="REVAi">REVAi</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Th!nk_City" title="Th!nk City" class="mw-redirect">Th!nk City</a> at a free parking and charging station in Oslo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Norway, with 10,005 plug-in electric cars registered through December 2012, is the country with the largest EV ownership per capita in the world, with <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> recognized as the EV capital of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2012_267-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2012-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwayLargest_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayLargest-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AVERE_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AVERE-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> A total of 2,240 cars were sold in 2011, up from 722 in 2010. Sales in 2011 were led by the <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_family" title="Mitsubishi i-MiEV family" class="mw-redirect">Mitsubishi i-MiEV family</a> with 1,477 units including 1,050 i-MiEVs, 217 Peugeot iOns and 210 Citroën C-Zeros, together representing 66% of electric car sales in Norway that year.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2011_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2011-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwayFleet1111_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwayFleet1111-302"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup> During 2012 a total of 4,679 <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_car" title="Plug-in electric car" class="mw-redirect">plug-in electric cars</a> were registered, including 318 <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> and 59 electric vans.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2012_267-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2012-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup> Electric-drive car sales in 2012 represented a 3.1% market share of passenger car sales in the country, up from 1.6% in 2011. Registrations in 2012 include 300 used electric vehicles imported, representing 1.0% of total used imports in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2012_267-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2012-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sales in 2012 were led by the <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">Nissan Leaf</a> with 2,487 units registered (including 189 used Leafs imported), and representing 53% of PEV sales in that year, reaching cumulative sales of 2,860 units since its launch in September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2012_267-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2012-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2011_12_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2011_12-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup> Norway is the only country in the world where an electric car has ranked among the top 10 best selling cars.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwaySales2011_12_303-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwaySales2011_12-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup> The Leaf continued in 2013 as the top selling plug-in electric car, with 1,049 units registered during the first quarter of 2013, including 199 used imports. During this quarter, the Nissan Leaf was the sixth best selling car in Norway.<sup id="cite_ref-Norway1Q2013_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norway1Q2013-304"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup><br style="clear:both;" /></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_subsidy">Government subsidy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Government subsidy">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_car&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Government subsidy" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles</a></div>
<p>Several countries have established <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">grants and tax credits</a> for the purchase of new electric cars depending on battery size. The U.S. offers a <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles#United_States" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">federal income tax credit</a> up to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$7,500</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-IRS2009_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRS2009-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> and several states have additional incentives.<sup id="cite_ref-PluginAm_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PluginAm-305"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup> The U.K. offers a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_Car_Grant" title="Plug-in Car Grant" class="mw-redirect">Plug-in Car Grant</a> up to a maximum of <span class="nowrap">GB£5,000</span> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$7,600</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of April 2011, 15 <a href="/wiki/European_Union_member_states" title="European Union member states" class="mw-redirect">European Union member states</a> provide <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles#Europe" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">economic incentives</a> for the purchase of new electrically chargeable vehicles, which consist of tax reductions and exemptions, as well as of bonus payments for buyers of all-electric and <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid vehicle" class="mw-redirect">plug-in hybrid vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid electric vehicles</a>, and some <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">alternative fuel vehicles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT072911_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT072911-308"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ACEA2_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACEA2-309"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup><br style="clear:both;" /></p>

<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web">Abuelsamid, Sam (2009-01-17). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.autoblog.com/2009/01/17/tesla-offers-laundry-list-of-new-options-12k-prepaid-battery-r/">"Tesla offers laundry list of new options, $12k prepaid battery replacement"</a>. Green.autoblog.com<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2010-07-16</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AElectric+car&amp;rft.au=Abuelsamid%2C+Sam&amp;rft.aufirst=Sam&amp;rft.aulast=Abuelsamid&amp;rft.btitle=Tesla+offers+laundry+list+of+new+options%2C+%2412k+prepaid+battery+replacement&amp;rft.date=2009-01-17&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fgreen.autoblog.com%2F2009%2F01%2F17%2Ftesla-offers-laundry-list-of-new-options-12k-prepaid-battery-r%2F&amp;rft.pub=Green.autoblog.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Agassi_TED_talk-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Agassi_TED_talk_92-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation audio-visual">Shai Agassi (2009-02). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ted.com/talks/shai_agassi_on_electric_cars.html"><i>Shai Agassi's bold plan for electric cars</i></a>. Long Beach and Palm Springs, California: TED conference. Event occurs at 4m10s<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2009-10-05</span>. "See we're bound by today's technology on batteries, which is about 120 miles if you want to stay within reasonable space and weight limitations. 120 miles is a good enough range for a lot of people. But you never want to get stuck. So what we added as a second element to our network is a battery swap system. You drive. You take your depleted battery out. A full battery comes on. And you drive on. You don't do it as a human being. You do it as a machine. It looks like a car wash. You come into your car wash. And a plate comes up, holds your battery, takes it out, puts it back in. Within two minutes you're back on the road. And you can go again. If you had charge spots everywhere, and you had battery swap stations everywhere, how often would you do it? And it ends up that you'd do swapping less times than you stop at a gas station. As a matter of fact, we add it to the contract. We said that if you stop to swap your battery more than 50 times a year we start paying you money because it's an inconvenience."</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AElectric+car&amp;rft.btitle=Shai+Agassi%27s+bold+plan+for+electric+cars&amp;rft.date=2009-02&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ted.com%2Ftalks%2Fshai_agassi_on_electric_cars.html&amp;rft.place=Long+Beach+and+Palm+Springs%2C+California&amp;rft.pub=TED+conference&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
